<div id="review_722332310" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722332310" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722332310?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006486039" href="/book/show/6662436-fool-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722332310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17309330951237541960">A good and satisfying ending to what has become my favourite Hobb trilogy. I thought the ending of the Farseer trilogy was good as well even though many didn’t find it a very fitting ending because a lot of Fitz’ pain and sacrifice went largely unrewarded and unrecognised. But I think even many of those critics would appreciate the end of this series.<br/><br/>Like the last book of the Farseer Trilogy, this book brings us to a dragon-centric quest. An adventure where the hero goes off to slay a dragon. We</span>
  <span id="freeText17309330951237541960" style="display:none">A good and satisfying ending to what has become my favourite Hobb trilogy. I thought the ending of the Farseer trilogy was good as well even though many didn’t find it a very fitting ending because a lot of Fitz’ pain and sacrifice went largely unrewarded and unrecognised. But I think even many of those critics would appreciate the end of this series.<br /><br />Like the last book of the Farseer Trilogy, this book brings us to a dragon-centric quest. An adventure where the hero goes off to slay a dragon. Well...that would have been a nice story. This story is a little different as Thick points out<br /><br /><i>“Adventure? Puking and eating fishy food? Going up and down, up and down, all the time? Going around people who wonder why I'm not dead?” He crossed his stubby arms on his chest. “I heard adventures in stories. Adventures have golden coins and magic and beautiful girls to kiss. Adventures aren't puking!”</i><br /><br />Poor Thick. Still, we do eventually get a story of dragons and dragon slayers and dragon savers and heroes and beautiful girls to kiss. However, again, most of the dramatic tension and climaxes are found in Fitz' navigation of his relationships and personal identity, more so than the larger events. The quests and physical action climax well before the end of the book but that doesn’t mean all the drama is finished. You may well still find yourself biting your nails and peeking through your fingers as Hobb brings all Fitz’ chickens home to roost. <br /><br />By now, Fans of the Fitz and Fool novels have come to expect that Hobb will treat Fitz harshly – and that there is no guarantee that he will get rewarded and recognised for every or even any good deed. Many may ask with a knowing grimace, “is this a happily ever after kind of story?” I would probably have to reply...of a sorts. You may be surprised. I found it very satisfying in any case. So much so that I have to think about how I feel about Hobbs recent announcement of a new Fitz and Fool trilogy in the making. Part of me leaps up at the thought of more stories from our dynamic duo – but part of me is happy to let things lie as they are – because I suspect more Fitz and Fool equals more pain, more suffering, more loss. Then again, with all those things come more risk, more love, <i>more life.</i> It would be a bit of an ask though for it to bring more than...<br /><br />5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17309330951237541960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006486039" href="/book/show/6662436-fool-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9653496-hanne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453422265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10449583509780785955"><i>A letter home - </i><br/><br/>That’s it then, another quest came to an end. Another set of mysteries explained. We went sailing (which Thick was very grateful for) and ice fishing, we made ice castles (though 'labyrinth' would probably cover it better) and we even made a dragon or two fly. The weather wasn't very good, and I probably hadn't packed enough Siberian-inspired winter clothes but I survived, somehow. The food wasn't really good either, but luckily I found an abandoned honey jar on the way.<br/><br/>As always</span>
  <span id="freeText10449583509780785955" style="display:none"><i>A letter home - </i><br /><br />That’s it then, another quest came to an end. Another set of mysteries explained. We went sailing (which Thick was very grateful for) and ice fishing, we made ice castles (though 'labyrinth' would probably cover it better) and we even made a dragon or two fly. The weather wasn't very good, and I probably hadn't packed enough Siberian-inspired winter clothes but I survived, somehow. The food wasn't really good either, but luckily I found an abandoned honey jar on the way.<br /><br />As always, I was in magnificent company though: Fitz is still my favourite, and I feel it important to note that he’s finally growing up and accepting some the responsibilities he refused to take for so long. Really, it was foolish of him to think you can decline your family heritage, or that you can leave people behind for so long without some consequences. <br /><br />I really enjoyed meeting Nettle, though I still think we didn’t see enough of her. Dutiful is becoming wiser every day, I think he’ll make a magnificent king. Then there is Thick, an absolutely wonderful human being, especially when he’s outsmarting the others. They continuously underestimate him, and that’s probably his biggest advantage. (I am consciously leaving Chade and the Fool out here – both of them rubbed me the wrong way this trip!)<br /><br />To be honest though, I think this was probably the least of our travels in this world so far. Don’t get me wrong, it was still bloody damn good, and worth every second or penny, but it wasn’t the big apotheosis I was aching for. <br /><br /><br />Cheers!<br />Hanne.<br /><br />PS: I’m sorry for not having written earlier. I was stuck somewhere in a skill pillar and time just whooshed by. But now, I’m on my way home and I’m bringing a dragon head with me. Please make sure you clear the landing space and have a few cows ready. You never know!<br /></span>

<div id="review_20806333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20806333" />
    <a title="Aidan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1109421-aidan"><img alt="Aidan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442972639p2/1109421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20806333?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aidan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aidan" href="/user/show/1109421-aidan">Aidan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6401606-fool-s-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20806333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7566777118938235939">So bittersweet. It's going to be hard for any book/series for the rest of the year to top the experience I had with the Tawny Man trilogy. I first read the Farseer trilogy when I was in my mid-teens, roughly Fitz's age through the trilogy. I connected to a lot of his conflicts. I'm now the same age as Fitz during the Tawny Man trilogy, and I think that helped the books resonate with me as an adult. I don't think I would have been able to connect with his challenges as a father (in several capaci</span>
  <span id="freeText7566777118938235939" style="display:none">So bittersweet. It's going to be hard for any book/series for the rest of the year to top the experience I had with the Tawny Man trilogy. I first read the Farseer trilogy when I was in my mid-teens, roughly Fitz's age through the trilogy. I connected to a lot of his conflicts. I'm now the same age as Fitz during the Tawny Man trilogy, and I think that helped the books resonate with me as an adult. I don't think I would have been able to connect with his challenges as a father (in several capacities) if I'd read the book in my 20s.<br /><br />Fitz's growing relationship with the Fool is perfect. It's a complex, romantic, empowering and believable bond between two real people. This is doubly effective since Fitz is a heterosexual man who has to navigate the Fool's labyrinthine feelings (romantic and otherwise) for him. I don't know that I've read any other relationship between non-romantically involved men that revolves singly around their love for one another. (Though, I'm also not sure that the Fool identifies as male. Especially considering the Liveship trilogy. The Fool's personas have genders.)<br /><br />In any case, it's an intricate, vulnerable, brave, and honest relationship that Hobb explores. It'll take time to reflect, but I think Tawny Man is even better than Farseer, which is a modern classic in its own right. Go read it all.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7566777118938235939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_929290044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929290044" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9146810-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581734604p2/9146810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/929290044?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/9146810-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive15_read-2015">z_archive15_read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=own-paperback">own-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer929290044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8529266670801361066">Recommendation: Buy this book(series) and make it top priority.<br/><br/>Fool’s Fate by Robin Hobb is the culmination of the Tawny Man Trilogy, a trilogy that got better with each book, and ended spectacularly with a lot of feeling. Fool’s Fate is the 9th book in Hobb’s Realm of the Elderling Series and those books need to be read before you read Fool’s Fate. Those trilogies are The Farseer Trilogy and The Liveship Traders Trilogy. This is an epic fantasy series that focuses on characterization and inter-</span>
  <span id="freeText8529266670801361066" style="display:none">Recommendation: Buy this book(series) and make it top priority.<br /><br />Fool’s Fate by Robin Hobb is the culmination of the Tawny Man Trilogy, a trilogy that got better with each book, and ended spectacularly with a lot of feeling. Fool’s Fate is the 9th book in Hobb’s Realm of the Elderling Series and those books need to be read before you read Fool’s Fate. Those trilogies are The Farseer Trilogy and The Liveship Traders Trilogy. This is an epic fantasy series that focuses on characterization and inter-personal relationships with a character that has many secrets from those individual relationships.<br /><br />Talking about the plot of this book would be a large spoiler for what happened in the previous books so I am going to be vague. Fool’s Fate has the Six Duchies people attempting to make a trading partnership with The Out Islander people but the prince of the Six Duchies must find a dragon frozen in ice to signify his worthiness to marry the Out Island princess. Fitz, from the shadows, must be the catalyst that changes events for the betterment of the entire realm. There is a lot of court characters and plotlines that run through multiple character. Hobb’s focus is on the inter-personal relationships that Fitz has.<br /><br />This book was just fantastic in every way. This is a trilogy that got better with each book, like a trilogy should do. The first book, Fool’s Errand, caught the reader and Fitz up with what is happening in the Six Duchies, and keeping secrets. The second book, Golden Fool, saw Fitz try to control other people and seeing his secrets unravel. In this last book, Fool’s Fate, we see Fitz finally succumbing to his fate, and letting his secrets go. Fitz is much more mature in this trilogy than the Farseer Trilogy and that makes him a more dynamic character. It is nice to read a group of books centered around a middle aged man instead of a teenager.<br /><br />The main focus of this trilogy is really inter-personal relationships and following a character that finally learns how to deal with his inter-personal relationships. There are a lot of secrets that could be deadly to know about. People in Fitz’ life are happy and if they knew the truth they might get hurt, so Fitz holds back a lot of the truth from his friends. Why this book and this series is so enjoyable is because we see the unraveling of all these secrets that Fitz holds from about a dozen other characters. Each person has a completely different relationship to Fitz, a varying degree of relationship. Based off of the level of their relationship, they know only certain things about Fitz. When the secrets or the hard decisions come up, these relationships are strained, causing great drama.<br /><br />The highlight of this book and the entire trilogy is Fitz’ relationship with The Fool. Their dynamic is the best dynamic in the entire series and their friendship is such an interesting thing to read about. There are so many dynamics to their relationship that makes each decision seem like something that holds the weight of the world on their shoulders. If you are looking for a series of fantasy books that has one of the best friendships ever written, check these books out.<br /><br />I loved this book because I felt so many emotions while reading this. After you read so many books about the same characters, there are these moments of interaction that you have been waiting for so many pages of text to see, so when it finally happens it is unbelievably moving. This was such an up and down emotional journey and a lot of these emotional sequences are happening during scenes of action and extreme plot development. In other words, I read scenes that were really exciting to only have this huge emotional response, but thrown right back into the excitement, and it was amazing. This happened a multiple of times and I love the ride that Hobb took me on.<br /><br /><b>5/5<br /><br />23/25 Possible Score<br /><br />Plot – 4(Strong)<br /><br />Characters – 5(Very Strong)<br /><br />Setting/World Building – 4(Strong)<br /><br />Writing Style – 5(Very Strong)<br /><br />Heart &amp; Mind Aspect – 5(Very Strong)</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8529266670801361066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14311280355115890461"><i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/54099-realms-of-the-elderlings' rel='nofollow noopener'>Realms of the Elderlings</a>
</i>, third series done and it’s getting better and better. <br/><br/>This last part from <i>Tawny Man</i> was incredible and the sun has risen, at last, on Fitz’ street. After around seven thousand pages I was finally rewarded! I felt that a stone lifted from my heart – that’s how good Robin Hobb writes.<br/><br/>But all these stories are not only about Fitz, the Fool, dragons and scheming. It goes deeper: it shows the human inner nature, one’ struggle with his thoughts and feelings, what it takes</span>
  <span id="freeText14311280355115890461" style="display:none"><i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/54099-realms-of-the-elderlings" rel="nofollow noopener">Realms of the Elderlings</a>
</i>, third series done and it’s getting better and better. <br /><br />This last part from <i>Tawny Man</i> was incredible and the sun has risen, at last, on Fitz’ street. After around seven thousand pages I was finally rewarded! I felt that a stone lifted from my heart – that’s how good Robin Hobb writes.<br /><br />But all these stories are not only about Fitz, the Fool, dragons and scheming. It goes deeper: it shows the human inner nature, one’ struggle with his thoughts and feelings, what it takes to make decisions and live with the consequences and what friendship and love truly means.<br /><br />And I didn’t mention before the love for animals which is present in her stories. You can feel her deep respect for nature and its creatures. Below fragment couldn’t be more accurate:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“No wolf wastes time on vengeance, and that is what this is. Vengeance, pure and simple. When people look most vicious, what you are seeing is not their animal side. It is savagery that only humans can muster. When you see me loyal to my family, then you see the wolf.”</i>
</blockquote> <br />I wish I had the Wit…<br /><br />After I read <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41452-farseer-trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">Farseer Trilogy</a>
</i> I said I will never become Hobb’s fan; well, I was wrong. So, never say never… :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14311280355115890461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h44LRrfXD3cwpZ8IRhiMLZH0gyCt4Sygb84pM9+BHERJErMKcfN6Mtg7NjHcH8Y9yjrG/WEaJV3aZqANTs5CFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9wZkJqaeI9xUxc+AG6J4H6H+UvbO1cY6nnZyrGjREzI5mtxqYLpWmbxbZrmBpTIP+jAXKwIuz8cr3vuS+Z5NYg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

But even at this westernmost edge of civilization, they can\'t rest for long---and they are soon back doing what they do best: stealing from the undeserving rich and pocketing the proceeds for themselves.\n\nThis time, however, they have targeted the grandest prize of all: the Sinspire, the most exclusive and heavily guarded gambling house in the world. Its nine floors attract the wealthiest clientele - and to rise to the top, one must impress with good credit, amusing behavior...and excruciatingly impeccable play. For there is one cardinal rule, enforced by Requin, the house\'s cold-blooded master: it is death to cheat at any game at the Sinspire.Brazenly undeterred, Locke and Jean have orchestrated an elaborate plan to lie, trick, and swindle their way up the nine floors...straight to Requin\'s teeming vault. Under the cloak of false identities, they meticulously make their climb - until they are closer to the spoils than ever.\n\nBut someone in Tal Verrar has uncovered the duo\'s secret. Someone from their past who has every intention of making the impudent criminals pay for their sins. Now it will take every ounce of cunning to save their mercenary souls.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17155283575889996653">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText17155283575889996653" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17155283575889996653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

With rich characters, breathtaking magic, and sweeping action, Golden Fool brings the reluctant adventurer further into the fray in an epic of sacrifice, salvation, and untold treachery.Golden FoolPrince Dutiful has been rescued from his Piebald kidnappers and the court has resumed its normal rhythms. But for FitzChivalry Farseer, a return to isolation is impossible. Though gutted by the loss of his wolf bondmate, Nighteyes, Fitz must take up residence at Buckkeep and resume his tasks as Chade’s apprentice assassin. Posing as Tom Badgerlock, bodyguard to Lord Golden, FitzChivalry becomes the eyes and ears behind the walls. And with his old mentor failing visibly, Fitz is forced to take on more burdens as he attempts to guide a kingdom straying closer to civil strife each day.The problems are legion. Prince Dutiful’s betrothal to the Narcheska Elliania of the Out Islands is fraught with tension, and the Narcheska herself appears to be hiding an array of secrets. Then, amid Piebald threats and the increasing persecution of the Witted, FitzChivalry must ensure that no one betrays the Prince’s secret—a secret that could topple the Farseer throne: that he, like Fitz, possesses the dread “beast magic.”Meanwhile, FitzChivalry must impart to the Prince his limited knowledge of the Skill: the hereditary and addictive magic of the Farseers. In the process, they discover within Buckkeep one who has a wild and powerful talent for it, and whose enmity for Fitz may have disastrous consequences for all.Only Fitz’s enduring friendship with the Fool brings him any solace. But even that is shattered when unexpected visitors from Bingtown reveal devastating secrets from the Fool’s past. Now, bereft of support and adrift in intrigue, Fitz’s biggest challenge may be simply to survive the inescapable and violent path that fate has laid out for him.From the Hardcover edition.<\/span>\n
